SILSOE v. MAULDEN.-The return match was played
in Wrest Park, Silsoe, on Thursday afternoon, Silsoe
again proving victorious by nearly 100 runs on the
first innings. For the winners, J. Gray made 30, M.
Squire 23, H. Squire 18, and A. Bottoms 16 not out.
Maulden were dismissed for 19, Gudgin taking 6
wickets for 6 runs, and Porter 3 for 10 runs. In their
second innings, Maulden compiled 37 for 8 wickets.

HOUGHTON C.C.: MARRIED v. SINGLE.-Played at
Houghton on Monday. Score:-Single, 39; Married,
100 for seven wickets.

MESSRS FORDER'S EMPLOYEES.-A match between
the employees of Sewell Lime Works and Blows Down
Lime Works was played at Houghton Green on
Saturday, and resulted in a win for the Sewell men by
one run, the scores being 61 and 60 respectively.

WATERLOW'S v ST. MATTHEW'S (LUTON).-Played
at Luton on Saturday. Score:-St. Matthew's, 61;
Waterlow's, 114.

DUNSTABLE 2ND XI. v. MARKYATE STREET.-
Played at Cheverells on Saturday. Rain considerably
interfered with the play, and when Dunstable had
made 76 for the loss of two wickets, the villagers
declared they had had enough of it, and stumps were
drawn.

DUNSTABLE SECOND ELEVEN v. MARKYATE STREET.
-This return match was played on the Cheverells Park
cricket ground, by kind permission of Mr. B. Bennett,
on Saturday. Dunstable had choice of innings and
batted first, Anderson and Elliott going to the wickets.
Four runs only had been scored when play was
interrupted by a heavy shower. After a while the game
was re-commenced, and a good stand was made by the
batsmen, the wickets being kept intact until 66 were
scored, when Elliott was dismissed, and Anderson
followed three runs later. Giddings and Beasley were
settling down for run getting, when play was again
interrupted for five minutes by a shower, at the end of
which the villagers refused to again take the field,
urging as an excuse that there was no likelihood of dis-
missing the Dunstable team that day. Not even the
promise to declare with 10 more runs added was sufficient
to induce them to take the field, and the game was
therefore left in the following position :-Dunstable-
W F Elliott, c and b Lee 27; C G Anderson, b Lee 34;
T Giddings, not out 5; J Beasley, not out 3; extras 7;
(2 wkts) 76.

DUNSTABLE BOROUGH GAZETTE: WEDNESDAY 14 AUGUST 1895 - 4.

OUR CAPTAIN.

MR L. C. R. THRING.
If there is one man to whom, more than others, Bedfordshire cricket owes its revival, and we might almost say its modern birth, that man is the genial and popular Head-master of the Dunstable Grammar School, Mr L. C. R. Thring. When, in 1888, the subject of our sketch took up his residence in our midst, the term "cricket" was practically a misnomer for the game which was played in what has often been called the "sleepy county." Save for the amateurish exhibitions with which we were favoured on our village greens, and the but little better exhibitions given by our town clubs, "ye manly olde game" had died a natural death. There was then no county cricket club, we could boast few really decent wielders of the willow, and as a county we were far in the rear as regarded England's national game. But better times were coming. Such a benighted state of affairs was intolerable to the indefatigable and energetic spirit whose life at that time became interwoven with ours, and not many months elapsed ere we humble Bedfordshire folk saw that a renaissance was dawning. Space will not permit us to follow minutely our worthy leader in his herculean task of reviving the all but dead pastime, suffice it to say that, mainly through his persistent efforts and untiring zeal, the game became once more established, the County Cricket Club was formed, and a county team of which from the first we have had cause to be proud, was put into the field.
Bearing these historical facts in mind, we came to the conclusion that a short biographical sketch of "our captain" would be of the greatest interest to our readers, and, fully intent on "button-holing" the ardent cricketer, we wended our way the other evening to the scene where he and such like spirits do congregate together. It was after a hard day's work behind the wickets, and when those tyrannical white-coated gentlemen had, to the relief of all parties concerned, reluctantly pocketed the balls, that we spotted our victim stalking in his manly, characteristic strides across the sodden turf. A neatly executed détour, and various winding oscillatory movements at last brought us into close quarters, and then, boldly running him to earth, with a decidedly menacing and aggressive air, we whipped out our note-book and pencil.
What a perfect horror some of our public favourites have of the interviewing fiend! And to what lengths will they not go in vain endeavours to avoid him? Thus it was with the subject of our sketch. Poor fellow! Had he but known half the uncanny means which Pressmen may call to their aid in order to attain their ends, he would at once have assumed that docile, martyr-like expression, and submitted like a gentleman to the trying ordeal.
"Ah, yes! I know what you want," (with a ghastly attempt at a smile). "I first saw the light at Uppingham in 1863, and from there ——"
"Half-a-minute, please. You were living at Uppingham ——"
"With my father, the Rev J. C. Thring, who was then Head Master of the Uppingham Grammar School. We remained there until I was two years of age, when we left for Bradford in Wiltshire."
"And your early education?"
"My earliest education was derived from my father. At nine years of age I returned to the Uppingham School, where the next four years of my life were spent. I left there at the time of the fever, and at 13 I was sent to Marlborough."
"It was here, I believe, you first learned cricket?"
"Quite so. Of course I had previously handled both bat and ball, but it was at Marlborough that I was grounded in the game. I met with fairly good success, and at 17 I was in the eleven."
"When did you play your first county cricket?"
"In 1880. I was playing in the Wiltshire team, and we were pitted against South Wales. I believe in my first innings I knocked up 20, but in my second venture only four came to my credit."
"But that was pretty good for a colt. From Marlborough you went to Cambridge?"
"Yes, that year I went to Cambridge, but I did very little at cricket there."
We knew the reason. It was our victim's innate modesty which led him to seek to hide the truth from us. But those who know anything about L. C. R.'s brilliant career at Cambridge will easily guess that he had very little time to waste over leather-hunting. But we let him have his way, and assuming an innocent look, continued :
"And where after Cambridge?"
"After leaving Cambridge I took a mastership at Wellingborough Grammar Schools. There I played a great deal of cricket. The masters' eleven was an exceptionally strong team. I went as master to Wellingborough in 1884, and I made more runs at Wellingborough than in any other period of my cricketing career."
"What was your top score there?"
"Well, as far as I can remember, it was when we were playing the Olney team. That day I scored 251."
"Ah, yes; and that is when you 'hit the top' as uncle Jonathan says. But now I think we will come to scenes nearer home."
"As you please. I came here in 1888. Soon afterwards the County Club was formed, and I have been hon sec. and captain of the team from its start."
This was really exasperating. We had hoped to hear the "governor's" account of how he brought about that happy state of affairs, and here he was glossing it over without a word about himself. But our victim was already showing signs of uneasiness, and fearing lest we should prematurely lose our prey, we waived the point.
"Is it not a fact that you have been at the top of our county batting averages every year since the club's inauguration?"
"That is quite so. My best performance in county cricket was last year, when we were trying conclusions with the M.C.C. I went in first on that occasion, and played through the whole of the innings, my record at the end being 127 not out."
"I believe you once saw F. W. Maude give a brilliant display of batting?"
"Yes. I was playing for Wiltshire against the M.C.C. when Maude made a century in each innings against us. In that match I met with my greatest success as a bowler. Eight wickets fell to my share for 40 runs, and this out of a total of 500 up against us."
"Which do you consider your best county season?"
"Well, taken as a whole, I think last year was about the best I have had yet. At one time last season I had made 580 runs for once out. I have not had such good luck this year."
But the subject of our sketch was fast becoming unmanageable. Making a desperate fight to the end we rapidly fired off our remaining questions :
"Height did you say? Well I am 5ft. 6in. I weigh about 11 stone, and really by nature I am 'not too inquisitive.'"
We took the gentle hint, and cordially thanking our genial captain for his courtesy, we departed.
A. W. M.

LUTON NEWS : THURSDAY 15 AUGUST 1895 - 5.

HYDE C.C. v. ST. MATTHEW'S.
This match was played on Saturday in the Park,
East Hyde, St. Matthew's winning by 32 runs.

A match was played at Churn Camp on Wednesday

on Saturday, between the local cricket eleven and a
Woburn team, resulting in a victory for the home team,
the scores being :—Hockliffe, 95 ; Woburn, 75.

DUNSTABLE BOROUGH GAZETTE: WEDNESDAY 21 AUGUST 1895-3.

DUNSTABLE TOWN FIRST ELEVEN v.
ASTON CLINTON.
Played at Aston Clinton on Tuesday, and resulted in
an easy win for the visitors by 146 runs. For the
winners Manton and Anderson made a splendid stand
for the first wicket, putting on no fewer than 104 runs
before being parted, when the former left for a grandly
played 67, the other principal scores being Giddings 36,
Staunton 32, Anderson 28, Pepper 24, and 30 standing
to the credit of "Mr Extras." The home wickets fell
very quickly before the bowling of W. F. Brown.
Langley for the home team batted well for 25, and a
stand of nearly an hour's duration was made by Chessall
and Pitt, but only 20 runs were added to the score, the
play during that time being very slow and monotonous.

TOWN SECOND ELEVEN v. CADDINGTON.
Played at Dunstable on Thursday, and ended in
a win for the home team by 24 runs on the first
innings. The batting of the visitors was exceed-
ingly feeble, the only one who seemed able to
play the bowling was Samm, who carried his bat
for 11; he also took five of the home wickets.
The runs for the winners were mainly from the
bats of three men—Anderson 15, Love 12, and
Marchant 16. In bowling Smith took seven for
18 runs, Gray two for 18. Score:—

TOWN SECOND ELEVEN v. CARTER'S C.C.
The town second eleven added one more to their
long list of victories, on Saturday last, on the
town ground, by defeating Carter's C.C. by 45
runs after a good game. The home batting was
fairly good, the principal scores being: Love 21,
Gray 21, Tompkins 14, Poulton 10, and Wright 13
(not out). On the visitors' side Bunker played
well for 21, as also did Mooring and Timm for 11
and 10 respectively. In bowling Giddings for
Carter's took six of the town wickets at a small
cost, while the wickets of the visitors were equally
divided among four of the home bowlers. Score:

DUNSTABLE VOLUNTEERS v. LUTON
DETACHMENT.
This match was played at Luton on Saturday,
and resulted in an easy win for Dunstable. Luton
batted first, and were all disposed of for 19 runs,
owing to the very successful bowling of Corporal
Smith. Dunstable scored 71, thus winning by 52
runs. The best scores for the winners were made
by Corporal Smith and Private Bunker (21 each).
The following comprised the Dunstable team:—
Colour Sergt. Elliott, Sergt. R. Hambling, Sergt.
W. D. Hambling, Corporal Smith, Private Bunker,
Private Sharratt, Private Bonham, Private Burch,
Private Darby.

READING OBSERVER : SATURDAY 25 MAY 1895 - 4

CRICKET.

IMPORTANT TO SECRETARIES.—As in former years, we readily grant a portion of our space for cricket match reports, but we must impress upon secretaries the importance of sending in the score as soon as possible after matches are played. We further desire to intimate that no score can be inserted unless it is written legibly and the innings set out in the form in which the matches are published. Sheets for drawing up reports can be obtained gratis on applying at the Observer Office. Notices of forthcoming matches will be inserted at the top of our cricket column at the rate of 1s. for each insertion. Match cards, posters and bills of all kinds are printed with the utmost despatch and on strictly reasonable terms at the Observer Office.

The eleven has played 23 matches, won 12, lost 6, and drawn 5, having scored 3,362 for 207 wickets, an average of 16.25 runs per wicket, against 2,371 for 232 wickets, an average of 10.22 per wicket, by their opponents. Four times they scored over 200, six times over 150, and six times over 100, whilst their rivals never reached 200, only five times exceeding 150, and six times exceeded 100. The highest score was 253 for 7 wickets, and the lowest 46. The highest score against them was 174 for 7 wickets, the lowest 25. R H Jackson has taken 14 catches at the wicket, while in the field H A Turner caught 10, A T Cliff and F W Parfitt 8, and F G Clarke and J Hodge 7.

[† Signifies not out].
Regarding the abilities of the players the following should prove of interest:—R. H. Jackson (1892-5) captain. Very useful behind the wicket, and is a smart catch; as a bat is steady, correct, and reliable, but not powerful.—J. Hodge (1892-5). A much-improved bowler, a brilliant field. A really good bat with a variety of strokes, but save for one excellent innings has lamentably failed.—A. T. Cliff (1893-5). Is an untiring bowler and has done some good performances. Very sound field. Bats with great nerve and hits hard and clean.—R. H. Morris (1893-5). Has improved somewhat in the last few matches, but earlier he showed nothing of his old form.—F. G. Clarke (1894-5). Very steady and most useful bat. Has fielded brilliantly at mid-off this season.—H. A. Turner (1894-5). Has not fulfilled his promise of last year; has, however, improved, and at times batted well. A fair and improving field.—P. L. Mousley (1894-5). Has abundantly justified expectations. Has a nice style and has played some excellent innings. A very clever cover-point.—F. Parfitt (1895). A painstaking bat with a nice off drive and a thoroughly reliable point. Is possessed of great promise.—W. Hatt (1895). A good left-handed bowler. Much improved in the field.—L. E. Todd (1895). A plucky bat, but lacks judgment. A good clean field when the ball comes straight to him, but does not start soon enough.—R. H. Mousley (1895). An erratic change bowler, very fair field and muscular bat.

READING STANDARD: FRIDAY AUGUST 9 1895-2.

BISCUIT FACTORY B XI v WHITE CROSS (BASINGSTOKE). —
On the Factory club ground on Saturday. The home team
batted first and ran up the respectable total of 131 runs,
mainly owing to the batting of Crook, Povey and Leaver, the
former especially punishing the bowling, he scoring no less
than seven 4's in succession. In the bowling department,
honours fell to W H Phillips, who took eight wickets for
eight runs in nine over. The visitors, on following on, made
a much better stand, scoring 51 for the loss of two wickets.

Wednesday, when a most enjoyable game resulted in a win

ALDERMASTON V. MORTIMER.—A closely contested game was
played in Aldermaston Park on Saturday between the Alder-
maston and Mortimer Clubs ; the home team won by three
runs. Owing to the heavy rains the wicket favoured the
bowlers, and in consequence the totals were small. For
Aldermaston Mr C. E. Keyser and E H. Ackerman obtained the
highest scores with 23 each. For Mortimer, Dobree, Wilson,
and Guilding secured double figures. Tea, fruit, and other
refreshments were, by the kindness of Mr and Mrs Keyser,
provided for the players and visitors who witnessed the game.

HEATH END V. ST. LAURENCE'S (READING).—At Heath End
on Saturday, the result of a highly enjoyable game being an
easy win for Heath End by 85 runs and two wickets. The
batting of Maxwell, White and W Hunt was exceedingly com-
mendable, Maxwell's innings of 72 runs being marred with
two mistakes only. The bowling of Maxwell and Roberts was
superb, Roberts' analysis reading seven overs, three maidens,
nine runs and five wickets ; and Maxwell's thirteen, four
maidens, fourteen runs and three wickets. After the match,
through the hospitality of Mr Hunt, the players partook of
tea on the lawn. At the conclusion of the meal the captain
of the home club (Mr E J Hunt), presented Mr H Roberts
with a cap in recognition of his recent performance of the hat

HIGHCLERE CASTLE V. HAMPSHIRE HOGS.—Played at High-
clere on Tuesday, the 23rd, when, thanks to the batting of
C. E. Slocock and J. A. Rutherford, the visitors were defeated
by 14 runs on the first innings. A. H. Evans, in the second
innings, registered a well-played 50. That the homesters were
victorious was largely owing to the effective bowling of Cave
and Evans. The only " Hogs " to reach double figures were
Major Clowes and F. R. Wilkinson. When the Major was
caught by Gosling, matters looked somewhat hopeful for the
Hampshire Hogs ; the " tail," however, cut up badly, and the
innings was finished off quickly for 14 runs. Score :—

GUILDHALL V NEWTOWN.—On the Newbury ground on Sat-
urday, and resulted in a win for the Guildhall by 75 runs on
the first innings. Guildhall, winning the toss, sent Pope and
Humphries to the wickets, but when the score was at 21,
Humphries was caught and bowled by Williamson. No
lengthy stand was then made until Edwards joined Pope ;
Edwards soon made 14. Drower was the only other man to
reach double figures ; and by free play he scored 22, the
innings closing for 102. Newtown, on handling the willow,
made a most disastrous start, six wickets falling for half-a-
dozen runs. Allsop was the best batsman, playing well for
his 18 not out. The innings closed for 27, Newtown being 60
runs behind their confrères. Allsop and Williamson at their
next venture played admirably, scoring between them 101
before being parted. Pope bowled well for G.C.C.,doing the hat
trick. Score :—

BERKSHIRE CHRONICLE. SATURDAY 10 AUGUST 1895-2.

READING CRICKET WEEK.

A new departure in connection with the Reading Cricket Club has been inaugurated this year in the direction of a cricket week. The matches have been played during the last few days, and the cricket week has been a conspicuous success. Reading have been able to rely on excellent teams for each of their matches, such powerful exponents of the summer pastime as Capt. Nepean, Mr L. G. A. Collins, Mr H. J. Collins, Mr W. O. Nares, Mr F. E. Chapman, Rev C. E. Chapman, F. W. Finch, F. Deane, rendering assistance, &c., and some interesting cricket has been witnessed.

FIRST MATCH-V. MARYLEBONE C.C.
The week opened with this annual fixture against the M.C.C. The visitors had the assistance of four professionals, Handford, Pike, Sherwin, and Rylott, and two members of the Reading Club, Mr P. T. Baker and Mr Wm. Greenfield. Mr C. T. Murdoch, M.P., captained the visiting team.
Inclement weather greatly interfered with the game, and it had to be finally abandoned. Reading went in first to bat, and thanks mainly to A. Finch (35), H. J. Collins (25), L. G. A. Collins (27), succeeded in compiling 186 runs for nine wickets, when they declared their innings closed. M.C.C. then went in, but after scoring 16 for one wicket, stumps were drawn owing to the rain. Mrs Murdoch kindly entertained the teams at lunch and tea. In addition to Mr Murdoch, M.P., Mrs Murdoch and party, there were present Mrs Arthur, and Mrs and Miss Pott, Mr Stanley Pott and party, the Misses Finch, Mrs James Simonds, Miss Maurice, Mrs W. C. Blandy, Mr Sidney Maurice, Mrs Hayward, Col. Taylor, &c. The following were the scores :-

SECOND MATCH-V. MR C. E. KEYSER'S XI.
Mr C. E. Keyser, of Aldermaston, who is an ardent cricketer, brought a strong team to Reading on Tuesday to play the local eleven. Mr Keyser's XI included C. E. Slocock, of Newbury, A. Finch, S. H. Maurice, and W. M. Greenfield, of Reading. Reading were successful in winning the toss, and their innings was remarkable for the fine display of batting by Mr L. G. A. Collins and Capt. Nepean, who made 151 and 108 respectively. When the score reached 301 Reading declared their innings closed. Mr Keyser's XI. began well, but the "rot" set in amongst the tail, and the innings closed for 105. Reading winning easily by 196 runs and four wickets. F. W. Finch took three wickets for 25 runs, Pott three for twenty, and Collins two for 4. The Reading Cricket Club provided lunch and tea for the teams. Amongst those present at the match were Major Mackenzie Edwards, Rev -- Gillum (Sonning), Colonel Taylor, Mr E. Sturges, Miss Garrard, Mr Claude Garrard, Mr J. H. Millard, the Misses Finch, Mrs James Simonds, and Miss Simonds. Scores :-

THIRD MATCH-V. MR W. HOWARD PALMER'S XI.-
This match was commenced on Wednesday on the Reading Biscuit Factory C.C. Ground. Reading had spared no effort in getting together a really powerful eleven, whilst Mr Palmer had whipped up an exceedingly strong team, including those well-known professionals, Bacon, of Hampshire, and Handford, of Notts. MAIDEN ERLEGH CRICKET WEEK.

READING STANDARD: FRIDAY 23 AUGUST 1895 - 2.

READING v. ABINGDON.—That the cricket field is one of the
favourite haunts of King Chance was evidenced beyond
doubt in this engagement, which was decided at Reading on
Saturday. On the occasion of the first match, played a short
time since at Abingdon, Reading were represented by a
fairly powerful combination, nevertheless they were the
recipients of a decisive thrashing. The Berks county
town, however, created a mild surprise in this en-
gagement, as despite that their eleven on paper was par-
ticularly weak they returned the compliment they received
at Abingdon with abject interest, inasmuch as they secured
more than an innings victory. The home captain ordered
his colleagues to the wicket first and before Crowhurst and
Campion ceased their partnership 41 runs had been obtained.
No serious advance in the figures was recorded before the
promising G Williams handled the willow, he going in
third wicket down. Between the third and fourth dismissal
82 chalks were added, but after that stage no rapid scoring
was chronicled, and when the umpires declared the homesters'
essay at a termination 143 was the total. Williams with
a score of 41 was the not out, the other chief
contributors being Crowhurst (17), Campion (28),
Pott (10) and E Eynott (11), each of whom
provided a good exhibition. On the visitors facing the attack
of Campion and Eynott, it was not difficult to forecast that
their fate was sealed after but a few minutes play. Dandridge,
who is generally looked upon a safe bat, was caught when one
run only had been compiled, and when three wickets were
down three chalks was the grand total. Lovett scored four-
teen, but in doing so had many fresh partners, as might be
gathered from the remark that at the fall of fourth wicket the
total was 12; five, 14; six, 18; seven, 26; eight, 29; nine, 31;
ten, 39. On following on, the visitors started in healthy style
as the first wicket realised 29. After this, however, the rot
noticeable in the first innings was again apparent, as the board
showed that in their second innings only 63 were compiled.
Of this number Dandridge notched 22 and A. B. Morland 13.
So successful did both Campion and H. Eynott trundle, that
the home captain was content to rely on the twain only in the
trundling department. That his judgment was sound was
demonstrated by the capital return chronicled, which is here
produced: Champion in the first innnings bowled 48 balls, and
secured one maiden and six wickets at a cost of twenty runs,
and in the second delivered 50 balls, and exact secured six
wickets for 34 runs. Eynott's analysis read: First innings,
nine overs, three maidens, 18 runs and four wickets. Second:
Twelve overs, three maidens, 25 runs, four wickets. Score:—

READING STANDARD: FRIDAY 23 AUGUST 1895-3.

GUILDHALL C.C. V NEWTOWN C.C. — These clubs met on Saturday in their return fixture at Sandleford park. The game, which ended in a win for Guildhall, was remarkable for low scoring, the bowlers taking everything before them, in addition to which the fielding of both sides was good. Humphries and Lucas for Guildhall bowled splendidly, the former capturing 12 wickets for as many runs, and the latter 7 for 8. Allsop and Williamson took the bowling honours for Newtown. The teams were entertained on the ground, and a hearty vote of thanks was accorded Lord Arthur and Lady Butler (who were present) for their kindness, also to Mr Allsop. Score :—

PARISH CHURCH INSTITUTE V HIGHCLERE.—The return match between these teams was played, by kind permission, on the cricket ground on Saturday in splendid weather. Highclere winning the toss decided to bat first, but owing to the bowling of Gunning and Gayfer, the first four wickets fell for 21, when Collins came in and made a useful stand, necessitating several changes in the bowling. At 70 runs came, Collins doing the lion's share, but Gunning going on at the top end fairly beat him with a beauty, whilst the Thirkills made some useful stands. After the interval the Institute started batting with Cook and Pyke, the former hitting his wicket, whilst Pyke contented himself by keeping up his wicket. Maslin, the next man, made things more lively putting on 18 in quick time. The others making double figures were Pyke, Young and Gunning. Both teams were entertained to tea, through the kindness of Miss L. Godding and Mr H Godding. Score :—

SPEEN V. BURGHCLERE.—This match was played at Speen on Saturday. Speen, winning the toss, sent Ashby and Freebody to the wickets, the former being unfortunately bowled, the ball hitting him on the chest and rebounding on to the wickets. A. Smith then joined Freebody and a long stand was made Speen putting on 148 before the innings was declared closed. Both Smith and Freebody played good cricket for their respective scores, 71 and 64. Burghclere then went in and totalled 63 before being dismissed. Sherman and Storie did best. Freebody was most successful with the ball, obtaining five wickets. Speen thus won a pleasant game by 85 runs and nine wickets. Score :—

LAMBOURN V HUNGERFORD.—A pleasant game was played on the Lambourn ground on Friday last between the Rev. J. E. Denning's eleven, and an eleven of the Lambourn club. The wicket was dead. After the recent rains, and was all in favour of the bowlers, Reed, who played for the visiting team, made sad havoc amongst the home team's wickets, "doing the hat" trick very prettily. F. Harris and V. Saunders were the only players to make any stand in the first innings, the first-named making 26 strokes for his score of 22. In the second innings Messrs H. J. Maberly and E. Bew did best, the first-named offering a stubborn resistance, against the good bowling, and carried his bat for 12. Messrs Bryant and R. Hobbs bowled well for Lambourn. EAST WOODHAY V. STOCKCROSS.—This, the return match, was played at Malverleys, East Woodhay, on Wednesday, the 14th inst, and after a pleasant game the visitors, for a second time this season, beat their opponents by 11 runs. S. J. Sturgess and F. Watkins shared the bowling honours, whilst S. Freebody (28) and Sturgess (11) were top scorers. The fielding of the visitors was very good; for East Woodhay H. Bastin was responsible for seven wickets and also put together 16 runs, whilst C. Thirkill played well for his 19 runs, also making 10 in his second venture and A. S. Carley, not out 10. NEWBURY V. 49TH REGIMENTAL DISTRICT.—The return match between these two elevens was played on Wednesday on the ground of the former in perfect cricket weather. The soldiers, who had got together a strong team, were the first to bat, Sergt. Crodine and Lieut. Corans facing the deliveries of H. D. Wells and W. Cave. The score increased steadily, and it was not until it had reached 73 that the first two batsmen were separated. When the sixth wicket went down, 111 was registered, but the rest of the men were quickly dismissed, and the whole side were all out before lunch for 142. Pte Smith, who showed fine form, was not out 28, his best hits being four four's, five three's, and ten two's, the only other batsmen to make a stand were Bromley (32), and Crodine (31). The home team opened their innings shortly after three o'clock, P. T. Hill and Cave opposing the bowling of Badding and Crodine, when runs came quickly. It was not until the telegraph board showed 75 that Middleton secured the professional's wicket. The retiring batsman had made 59 by some good cricket. H. D. Wells went in and Hill was directly afterwards bowled by Bromley. Two for 76. Ingram joined Wells and the two completely mastered the bowling, the result being that the visitors' score was passed just before five o'clock. Wells still continued to hit freely, and though several changes of bowling were tried they failed to bring about the desired effect. Stumps had to be drawn at 6-15 owing to the Reading men having to leave by the 6-34 train, the score standing at 193 for two wickets. The two not-outs Wells (62) and Ingram (43) gave a fine display of batting. They were at the wickets just over an hour, during which time they put on 118 runs. The match was watched with interest by a fairly large number of on-lookers. Score :—
49th Regt District    Newbury

ABINGDON HERALD : SATURDAY 7 SEPTEMBER 1895

ABINGDON CRICKET AND FOOTBALL
CLUB.
CRICKET SEASON, 1895.

Matches arranged: 21 ; played, 17 ; won, 8 ; lost, 7 ; drawn, 2 ; scratched, 4. The averages of the 1st XI. in both batting and bowling are appended:
It will be noticed that the late captain, Mr. F. D. Curtis, heads the batting list with an average of 24.50. Payne and Wilson coming next with 16.33 and 16.25 respectively, while Dandridge, Allen, W. Legge, F. H. Pryce and Skurray all get into double figures. Messrs. A. C. M. Croome and F. Deane appeared once each, and scored over the century, 117 being Mr. Croome's score and 109 Mr. Deane's. In the bowling Payne, Dandridge and H. S. Challenor have borne the brunt, the former taking 27 wickets at an average cost of 5.37 runs, Dandridge 49 at an average of 7.97 runs, and Challenor 37 wickets at an average of 9.02 ; all very good performances. Messrs. W. T. Morland, Wilson, Lovett, Legge and Ward have all rendered useful service in this department. Though the 1st XI. have achieved successes over Oxford City and Reading, they have not done so well generally, as in other years. The worst feature of this year's proceedings is the number of matches scratched. This we consider a bad omen for the club, as the reason given for the scratchings is the inability of the officials to raise teams. This ought not to be with any club having so many playing members on the books. Each member is supplied with a fixture-list at the beginning of the season, and as the success of the club should be the first thought of all members we greatly wonder at so many members engaging to play other matches on dates fixed for the club matches, but to this can be traced the falling off in the 1st XI. performances. If all the subscribing members would pull together, the Abingdon Cricket and Football Club would never lack a team, either 1st or 2nd, that would fail to uphold the honour of the club and the town which supports it, and we hope in future there will be no difficulty in this particular direction. We heartily congratulate the club on the success it has so far achieved and the members may be assured that if the remedies prescribed are properly applied there is a brilliant future in store.

THE SECOND ELEVEN
although not so successful this year as last, have been able to win more matches than they have lost, and in three cases out of five, had time permitted the drawn games to be played out the gains would most probably have been increased. The batting averages show a slight falling off. Jackson, who last year had an average of 22, takes second place with 15, but Glanville and Steptoe show marked improvement. Heath carries off the honours, but he has only played in six innings. There are several young players who claim attention, and it would be well for older members next season to look to these rising batsmen if they wish the club to prosper. Matcham, who only played three innings, was not out on each occasion, and winds up with an average of 58. In the bowling department a word of commendation is due to Glanville, who has bowled admirably. Heath and Pryce have both bowled well. If a great deal of the net practice was abolished and scratch teams were got together to practice, the fielding would be better. An improvement in that respect is much needed, for if the fielding had been smarter several matches could have been pulled out of the fire this season. Matches played, 12; won, 4; lost, 3; drawn, 5.

NEWBURY WEEKLY NEWS: THURSDAY 12 SEPTEMBER 1895-1.

NEWBURY CRICKET CLUB, 1895.

Thirty matches were arranged, of which 22 only were played; eight were scratched (six by opponents two by Newbury). The General Election caused Newbury to scratch their two. Of the matches played 15 were won, 4 were lost, and 3 drawn. A record was established by Newbury winning their last six matches consecutively, which included every match (five in number) in the cricket week. Mr. C. E. Slocock's 56 wickets for 8.23 runs per wicket was a very fine performance. In the six last matches (including the cricket week ones) the players were all bona-fide members of the Newbury Cricket Club, and with very few exceptions were local men. The captain (Mr. J. L. Flint) is entitled to a word of praise. It is no doubt greatly due to his tact and knowledge of the members and of their capabilities, that the club did so well. The teams have, so far as one can judge, never done otherwise than played together in a thoroughly good and sportsmanlike spirit, the result showing that "unity is strength."

NEWBURY WEEKLY NEWS. Thursday 12 SEPTEMBER 1895-2

CRICKET.

MR. SHEPHERD'S XI. beat WOOLLEY PARK.
This match was played at Woolley Park, on Wednesday. Woolley going in first put together the total of 67, of which Hayden and Smith did best, with 17 and 14 respectively. Mr. Shepherd's team then went to the score at lunch time standing at 21 for 8 wickets, Hutchins and Weaver playing good cricket for their runs. The innings closed for 82, Woolley going in again put on 58. Mr. Shepherd's team now required 33 runs to win, obtained them with the loss of 3 wickets, Hutchins again doing well. Both teams were kindly entertained to tea after the match by Mr. Wroughton. Score:

INKPEN beat FALKLAND C.C.
The visitors to meet the Inkpen C.C. on their own ground were rather late in coming, the time fixed for the match being two o'clock, while the game did not commence till about four. The home team won the toss and play quickly began. The chances of winning looked rather small at one time, four wickets having fell for 10 runs. E. Bance soon turned the tide by adding 19 runs in a very capital style, his score consisting of a splendid drive for 5, 2, 4, two 3's, and the rest singles. The Rev. H. D. Butler made a good hit for 4, and when the innings was closed carried out his bat. G. Butler and J. Hopkins did not bat. The visitors were dismissed for 29 runs, mainly owing to the first-rate bowling of T. May, who took 7 wickets, his average being 1.9. Score:-

LAMBOURN beat CHILTON.
The return match was played on Saturday last, on the Lambourn ground, and, as the score will show, resulted in a win for Lambourn, the homesters thus avenging their defeat in the previous match. The game did not commence till rather late, and consequently had to be decided on the first innings. The weather was delightful and the wicket really good. Chilton won the toss, but elected to send the home team in. A very poor start was made, as two Lambourn wickets went down for 0, but a wonderfully different complexion was put on the game, when, after H. Penfold had scored seven in good style, F. Harris and J. Bryant got well set. F. Harris made some splendid hits, and the spectators loudly cheered his plucky play, his score of 35 being made in a very short time. J. Bryant played capital cricket for his 38, and was greatly applauded upon his retirement. V. Hobbs and C. J. Maberly rendered great assistance to the score, before the innings was declared closed at 129. The Chilton team did but little, only one player (S. Panting) obtaining double figures. The bowling of Messrs. Hobbs and Bryant was very effective, and F. Harris made two capital catches in the long field. Chilton followed on, and at the call of time no wicket had fallen, the score being 43, H. New and Rumball having scored well during the innings. Score:-

In the second innings of Chilton, H New scored 21 (not out) and Rumball, 38 (not out); extras, 2; total, 61, for no wicket.

SOUTHINGTON beat MR. A. KINGSMILL'S XII.
This highly exciting and closely contested match was played in lovely weather on the observably situated Sydmonton Cricket Ground by youthful enthusiasts, the age being limited to 16, several, however, had many years still before them ere they reach this degree of experience. We would draw attention to the excellent bowling on the Southington side of Kneller and Poynter, and the batting of these and also Christie and North. The rest of the Sydmonton team was J. Chute whose bowling was as energetic as his batting, and his prowess was rewarded by the presentation bat offered for the highest score by Mr. Wyndham Portal. Leyland and Harrison had some share in the downfall of the Southington wickets, aided by the smart wicket-keeping of Andrew Kingsmill, in spite of their strenuous exertions Southington proved successful by the narrow margin of seven runs. BURGHCLERE beat NEWTOWN.
Played on the Sandleford Priory ground and ended in a defeat for the home team. Burghclere won the toss and batted first; three wickets fell quickly, but on Rev. G. Hicks and G. Kimber getting together runs were piled on fast, Kimber being run out for a well-played 13, Rev. G. Hicks carrying out his bat for a brilliantly-hit innings of 65. Newtown made no stand whatever, being all dismissed for 41, Allsop alone getting double figures. This match brought the Newtown season to a close, after a fairly successful season, they having played 14 matches, won six and lost eight. After a very disastrous start they pulled up in their last fixtures, winning three out of their last five. Score:-

NEWTOWN beat PARISH CHURCH INSTITUTE.
This return match was played in the beautiful grounds of Sandleford Park, on Saturday, August 31st, there being a goodly number of spectators present, including Lady Butler and family and company. Newtown went first to the wickets, and by good play and hard hitting on the part of Fidelil (22), and Gardiner (13), made a total of 48 runs, Gunning's bowling being too good for them, he being well backed up by Mathews and Fawcett. On the Institute handling the willow, however, they were soon disposed of for 30 runs, Vickers being top scorer with 16, Gibbs, Fidelil, Allsop, and Baverstock being the bowlers. Tea was then partaken of, and Newtown again went to the wickets, but the Institute not being able to go in again, the home team won a pleasant game on the first innings by eight runs.

ADBURY HOUSE beat NEWTOWN HOUSE.
On Thursday afternoon a match was played between elevens of the Adbury House estate and Newtown House, the game being won by the Adbury House eleven, a result being mainly due to the good bowling of H. Barber, F. James, and J. Gasson; G. Cooper brought off a beautiful catch at short slip, and S. Berry made a big drive for five runs. For the losers M. Stratford, White, Street, and Waight acquitted themselves very well. A capital tea had been prepared by the housekeeper on the grounds, which the players did justice too. Altogether a most enjoyable afternoon was spent, and a hearty vote of thanks was carried with acclaim to Mr. Walter Arkwright for his kindness. Score:

C R I C K E T .
HECKFIELD v. MAJOR MILDMAY'S XI.—Played at High-
field Park, Heckfield, on September 10, and resulted in
an easy victory for the home team, a fact mainly due
to an excellent innings by Bye, marred only by a single
chance. For the visitors, Major Mildmay played sound
cricket for twenty-seven. A large and fashionable gather-
ing watched the game with much interest. Score:
Heckfield: Rev H. Salter, 6—37; E Barnes, 8—5; I.
Bradfield, 5—12; J. Bye, 59 (not out)—10; Rev G. S.
Davies,0—2; F. H. Mauterin, 1—2; P. F. Law,8—4 (not
out); C. A. Law. 0—6(not out); W. H. P. Law, 0; A.
Doud, 24—18; Dr Comber,2; extras, 4 -1, Totals, 117
and 101 (for seven wickets).
Major Mildmay's XI: E. Bragley,5; C. Armiger,0; L.
Warren, 6; Major Mildmay. 27; P. Mildmay, 2; Rev J.
Saunderson, 0; G. Mildmay, 0; W. G. Cope, 8; M. L.
Cope, 0; A. White, 4; J. Pavey (not out), 0; extras, 7.
Total, 59.

FARINGDON ADVERTISER: SATURDAY 2 NOVEMBER 1895.

CRICKET CLUB—The annual dinner of the Lechlade Cricket Club, was held at the New Inn Hotel, on Thursday evening last. About 24 members and friends sat down to the very excellent repast provided by Mrs Richens, to which ample justice was done. The proceedings were presided over by Mr R. W. Prior-Wandesford, who was supported by Captain Tosswill, Dr. J. O. March, Mr W. Crosland, the vice-chair being occupied by Mr H. Milward. It being the first time the president had been present at the dinner, he most generously provided after dinner a very old-fashioned but acceptable drink viz., "rum punch," with which the toasts were drunk. The following was the toast list. "The Queen," by the chairman, "The President," by Mr H. Milward, responded to by the chairman, "Lechlade Cricket Club," by the chairman, responded to by Mr S. Campbell and Mr G. A. Davis, who, as is usual, read the averages for batting and bowling during the season, "Donor of Prizes," by Mr Davis, responded to by Mr H. Milward and Mr S. Campbell, "Tradesmen of Lechlade," by Captain Tosswill, responded to by Mr F. Stroud, "The Visitors," by Mr Crosland, responded to by Dr. J. O. March, "The Ladies," by Mr T. Slatter, responded to by Mr E. Bowley, "Mrs Richens," by Mr B. F. Innocent, responded to by Mr Richens, "Vice-President" (Mr H. Milward), by the chairman, "Captain," by Mr Davis, responded to by Mr B. F. Innocent. During the evening, Mr Campbell and Mr Milward presented the bat and ball, which was won by Mr W. Johns, to his father, Mr J. Johns, to be forwarded. Some capital songs were sung by the following—Captain Tosswill, Mr W. Crosland, Messrs. B. E. Innocent, Gibbs, Hudson, and Davis.

BRECON AND RADNOR COUNTY TIMES : FRIDAY 30 AUGUST 1895 - 2.

LOCAL SPORT.
CRICKET--BRECON v. LLANDOVERY.
This match was played at Llandovery on Wednesday the 21st inst. Brecon batted first and made a poor show, being all dismissed for 49. D. T. M. Jones took 6 wickets for 20. Llandovery were dismissed for the comparatively small total of 95, W. Ll. Thomas taking most of the wickets. Brecon fared little better in their second innings, being only able to compile 52. This left Llandovery 7 to win, and they lost 3 wickets before they got that number. The wicket was in a very bad condition and played badly. Scores:--
BRECON--1ST INNINGS.
T. Williams c Prytherch, b C.P. Lewis ...... 10

The Wycombe Y.M.C.A. C.C. play Newland Bible Class on
the Rye to-morrow (Saturday). Wickets pitched at 2.30.
Wycombe First XI. have no fixture for to-morrow, but the
Reserves go to Marlow to play Borlase School (return). On
Thursday—not Wednesday as at first arranged—the Grammar
School Past and Present play the Wycombe Club, on which
occasion we hear that Mr. and Mrs. Peachell have kindly
offered to provide luncheon and tea for the teams. This match
ought to prove a good even game, as several of the Club's First
XI. are old boys and will play for the School. We also hear
that on Saturday week, when the final in the Bostick Cup
Competition takes place, the Vicar and Mrs. Shaw intend
inviting all the members of the Club to partake of tea. Mrs.
Shaw has consented to present the Cup and medals at the
conclusion of the game, but we shall be able next week to give
fuller details of the arrangements for the day.
St. John's C.C. play the West End United on the Recrea-
tion Ground to-morrow at 2.30.—St. John's C.C. want
matches for the Saturdays in August.—R. Ford, West End-
road, Wycombe.
Church Room C.C. play Wheeler End Blue Star, at Wheeler
End, to-morrow, at 2.30.

SOUTH BUCKS FREE PRESS: FRIDAY 9 AUGUST 1895 - 3

HIGH WYCOMBE v. MR. E. STEVENS' XI.
On Saturday Mr. Edmund Stevens, of The Vache, Chalfont St. Giles, brought over a strong team to oppose the local club, but rain prevented the game from being played out. It was, however, drawn in favour of Wycombe, who had made 43 for the loss of two wickets, when stumps were drawn. No play was possible before luncheon, and a start was not made till past 3 o'clock, when the visitors went to the wicket. Before their innings was concluded, a smart shower compelled them to make a precipitate rush to the friendly shelter of the pavilion. The rain holding off for a time allowed the innings to be finished, 57 runs being the result. On Wycombe going in the light was very bad, and the rain came down at intervals in torrents, so that after several attempts to play out time it was thought best to leave the game drawn. At that point the match was left in the position shown by the following score and analysis. The wet did not hinder Baines from making some good strokes, his 29 including a 5, two 4's, three 3's, and two 2's:-

RAYNERS XI v. PERMANENT STAFF OF THE 3RD BATT. OXFORD LIGHT INFANTRY.
On Monday last, August 5th, a match was played on Rayners private ground, between the above teams, and, after being hindered a little by the unsettled weather, ended in a decisive victory for the former by an innings and 11 runs. Mr. C. M. Rose captained the home eleven, and, having won the toss, elected to bat. The game was very slow at the commencement, and 4 good wickets were lost for 21, but when the captain and Mr. Powell became associated, the best stand of the day was made, and some good cricket was seen, both playing with confidence. They put on 64 runs between them, when Mr. Rose was caught at the wicket for an invaluable 37. Powell left soon after with a well-played 29 to his credit. Wheeler made 14, and the remaining batsmen being quickly disposed of, the innings closed for 114. An adjournment was now made for lunch, which had been prepared (in a spacious marquee, erected for the occasion) through the generosity of Sir Philip and Lady Rose. After ample justice had been done to the good things provided, the visitors commenced their innings. Captain Rose and Bugler Wakelin were the only ones to show any resistance to the attack of C. M. Rose and Powell, who were bowling in their best form, and the innings closed for 51. Captain Rose's 15 was far and away the best batting display, which included one 5, a clean drive out of the ground. Powell had the best analysis, taking 6 wickets for 23, while Mr. Rose's 4 cost 25 runs. Having to follow on, they failed to reach the number required to save an innings' defeat, Dean taking 6 wickets for 12 runs, and the game resulted as before stated. Full score and analysis:-

BURNHAM v. FLACKWELL HEATH.
This match was down for decision at Burnham on Saturday. Rain, however, prevented its being played out. Burnham winning the toss, Tilbury put his men in first; and though a start could not be made before 4 o'clock, they knocked up 127 runs for the loss of 8 wickets when play ceased. Tilbury scored 42 (not out), F. T. Santer 27, R. Brant 12, and F. W. Baker 11. Low (5 for 41) and B. W. Soper (2 for 13) were the successful bowlers. Score:-

MARLOW v. ORIEL.
Played at Marlow on Monday in very showery weather. The local club found it difficult to raise a side, and but for some help from Wycombe, would probably have had to play short. The team which took the field included H. H. Morris, who is staying in Marlow, the bowling being the weak point. Marlow won the toss and batted. Massie, Langley, and T. Thurlow all compiled useful scores, but the stand of the innings was made by Bowe and Barton, who carried the score from 112 for eight wickets to 173 for nine. Barton hit a six, three 4's, and two 3's in his 39. The innings closed for 176. The visitors made an excellent start with Arundel and H. C. Owens. Runs came steadily from the bowling of Massie and Coleman, and 70 went up before Baillie effected a separation by catching Owens off his own bowling. Afterwards the Oriel men did badly. Arundel was run out at 85, bowled by Coleman. His dashing innings of 54 included a 6, six 4's, a 3, etc. Langley took up the bowling with the total at 107 for four wickets and met with great success, securing five of the last six wickets at a cost of 15 runs. The innings closed for 136, and Marlow therefore won by 40 runs. Score and analysis:-

SOUTH BUCKS FREE PRESS : FRIDAY 9 AUGUST 1895 - 4

Cricket.
(Other news on page 6).

WYCOMBE v. ORIEL.
A team from which Fred Langley, Bird, Baines, Mumford,
Raffety, and the Rev. E. D. Shaw were absentees did not look
on paper strong enough to do battle successfully for Wycombe
when they had to meet the Oriel club on Tuesday. However,
with the assistance of C. Langley and G. Langley—the latter
playing for his brother—and W. Stone, a Wycombe man,
who, since his residence in the Midlands, has been tried in
the Warwickshire Colts' team, they managed to win on the
first innings by 47 runs, to which Keen contributed 33 and
Stone 22, and four other batsmen also got into double figures,
so that when the last wicket fell the total had reached 131.
Unfortunately Page was unable to bowl, having twisted his
knee in turning to make his last run; but Keen and G.
Langley bowled with such effect that Reid and W. R. Percival
were the only two among the visitors who made anything
approaching a stand against their deliveries, and the whole
side were disposed of for 84. The bowling of the Oriel men
in Wycombe's second innings was somewhat loose, and got
severely punished, as shown by the subjoined score and
analysis:—

This match was played on the Wycombe Rye on Monday
last, resulting in a win for the Y.M.C.A. by 8 wickets. The

Hoing (10) being principal contributors. The Y.M.C.A. then

Y.M.C.A. play St. Anne's C.C. on the Rye next Saturday,

WYCOMBE MARSH F.C.—A general meeting of the above
was held on Tuesday, July 30, to consider if they should enter
the Junior League, when after some discussion it was proposed
and carried. It was decided to adjourn the meeting until
August 13th, at the Red Lion, at 8 o'clock. All members are
requested to attend, as the business will be election of officers,
&c., for the next season.

CHALFONT PARK v. ST. SILAS (LONDON).—The annual
match was played between the above, at Chalfont Park, on
the 5th, and resulted in a win for the home team, who are to
be congratulated, considering the number they had to con-
tend with (21). Sidney Golding played excellent cricket, 21
not out in the first and 24 in the second innings. Cox bowled
capitally, taking 16 wickets for 13 runs. The visitors' scoring
was very low; Austin bowled fairly well for them. Chalfont
made 36 in the first innings and 111 for six wickets in the
second. The visitors' twenty-one were all got rid of for 32.

BURNHAM v. POSTAL TELEGRAPH (LONDON).—This match
was played at Burnham on Monday last, when the visitors
won a game which, except for the weather, was a very pleasant
one. Burnham batted first, but were all out for 47—Tilbury
11, Santer 16 (not out), and Painter 10. James bowled
splendidly, taking 6 for 20 runs, Muckle 3 for 14, and Milner
1 for 10. The Postal team fared better than their opponents,
knocking up 83, W. Milner (23) and Bordeaux (25) doing
best. Baldwin took 6 for 24 and Santer 4 for 16. Going in
again, Burnham scored 61 for the loss of 4 wickets and then
declared; Baker (26 not out), Woodley (16), Baldwin (14), and
Hall (12 not out) batted in fine form. Rain, however, stopped
further play, and the Telegraph Staff thus won by 36 runs on
the first innings. Muckle captured 3 wickets for 36 runs.

TAPLOW STATION v. BRYANSTON-SQUARE.—Played on the
Station Ground on Saturday, the homesters winning easily.
After disposing of the visitors for 52 (F. Smith 13), Taplow
scored 59 for 6 wickets when the game was stopped by rain.
H. Painter made 15, G. Jones 10 not out, and C.Frost 10. For
the winners Fisher obtained 7 wickets for 20 runs, Frost 3 for
1, and J. Wright 1 for 10. For Bryanston Rowland (5 for 15
and Garrett (1 for 19) were the successful trundlers.

COLHAM GREEN v. GERRARDS CROSS.—This popular match
was played on the charming ground at Evelyns. Showery
weather somewhat interfered with the game and only one
innings each was played. The visitors scored 69; Gerrards
Cross put together 117 and won by 48 runs. Captain Penton
made 34 and G. Lewis 26 for the home team. Mrs. Worsley's
hospitality to the players was much appreciated.

SOUTH BUCKS FREE PRESS: FRIDAY 16 AUGUST 1895 - 4.

FLACKWELL HEATH 2ND XI. v. LITTLE MARLOW.
LOW SCORING.
A match between the above clubs was played on the ground of the latter on Saturday last, and resulted in a victory for Flackwell Heath by 25 runs on the first innings. The batting of Musk, Baker, and Smith was very good. Almond accomplished the hat trick, taking 3 wickets in 3 successive balls. Clifford also bowled well. The second innings of the latter proved most disastrous, they being dismissed in 20 minutes for 9 runs. No doubt the result would have been different had time permitted a second innings for the visitors. Davis and Penny batted in good form. In the second innings of Flackwell Heath Almond again accomplished the hat trick, and took 6 wickets for 1 run. Penny obtained 4 for 6 runs. Score:—

MARLOW v. HIGH WYCOMBE.
BIG HITTING BY H. H. MASSIE.
The return match between these old rivals was played at Marlow, on Saturday, in fine weather, on a wicket that favoured the bowlers. It will be remembered that the first match at Wycombe was left drawn much in favour of Marlow. On this occasion the riverside town gained an easy victory, thanks to a fine innings by H. H. Massie, the Australian batsman (who is staying at Marlow this summer), and some excellent bowling by W. H. Lunnon and Barber. Marlow won the toss, Langley and Barber facing the deliveries of Page and H. S. Parker. Runs came steadily until the total reached 30, when both batsmen were out with a dozen to their credit. Massie and Lunnon advanced the total to 56, when the latter was caught by White, and as Baillie failed to score, and Want only hit a 4, five wickets were down for 65. Bower then came to the aid of Massie, and a useful stand was effected. The 110 went up amidst cheers, but with four added a great change came over the game, H. S. Parker sending back Brower, Burton, and Mackenzie in one over. Six, seven, and eight for 104. Massie was now hitting with tremendous force, and was especially severe on Page, a gigantic hit for 6 into Court Garden delighting the onlookers hugely. Morgan batted steadily while the Australian hit until the total was 140, when he was yorked by Parker. Just when it appeared certain that Massie would take out his bat he was captured in the slips, and the innings closed for 146. Massie's dashing score of 69 included two 6's, eight 4's, two 3's, and eight 2's. He was deservedly applauded on retiring to the pavilion. Both Parker and Keen bowled well. Wycombe commenced their innings with F. M. Parker and Langley. The bowlers were W. H. Lunnon and Barber. A more disastrous start could not well be imagined. Lunnon caught and bowled Parker and clean bowled Baines in his first over. Two for 0. G. George scored a couple of singles, and Langley was then caught by Mackenzie off Barber. Three for 2. H. S. Parker helped George to put a better aspect upon affairs, but the former was out at 22, after hitting up 16. Janes followed in and was bowled by Lunnon at 28. The brothers George then got together and carried the score to 40, when three wickets fell—the George brothers and White, all clean bowled. Page hit up 14 by means of a 6, a 4, and two 2's, and the innings closed for 60. Lunnon bowled uncommonly well, his seven wickets costing 32 runs each. Wycombe followed on, and made 50 for one wicket. Langley batted well for 25 not out. Marlow therefore won by 86 runs on the first innings—a rather unexpected result, seeing that the team which was in the field was by no means a strong one. Score and analysis:—

COLESHILL C.C. v. ST. MARGARET'S C.C.
The return match between the above clubs was played at Coleshill on Saturday, August 10th. St. Margaret's again proving successful, which was chiefly owing to the brilliant all-round cricket of Mr. C. C. Powell, who not only made the highest score for his side, but actually took 5 wickets for 6 runs. Mr. J. Dean also bowled wonderfully well, taking the other 5 for 20 runs. Coleshill went to the wickets first, and were soon disposed of, Mr. R. M. Weatherby being top scorer with 11, and the innings closed for 29. St. Margaret's now commenced their task of making 30 to win, which was soon accomplished. Fountain made 11; Mr. Powell made 21, which was compiled without the slightest chance, and the innings realized 78. Coleshill went to the wickets a second time, and did much better, having made 73 for 5 wickets when time was called. Full score and analysis:--

WYCOMBE RESERVES v. WEST WYCOMBE.
This match was played at West Wycombe on Saturday afternoon. The visitors went to the wicket first, but offered a very feeble resistance to the bowling of Turner and Fletcher, who each took five wickets for 10 runs. The home side, owing to the good batting of Turner, A. Harman, and Fletcher, reached a total of 79. For the Reserves Keen bowled in good form, taking six wickets for 23 runs. In their second attempt the Reserves did better, and passed their former score before the third wicket fell; but their total was not high enough to avert defeat, as it left the home side only 32 to get to win, which they accomplished with the loss of four wickets. HIGH WYCOMBE v. WOOBURN INSTITUTE.
This match, which was played on the Wycombe ground last Saturday afternoon, resulted in a draw that, if time had permitted, would have ended in favour of the home team. The visitors were without Bayley, the Lansons, and others who generally play for the Institute; but they had the assistance of H. Bacon, who proved a tower of strength to them in both departments of the game. Wycombe did not play their full strength, more than half their number being reserve men. The home side went in first, and a total of 156 was reached before they were all disposed of. The chief contributor to this score was F. George, whose figures included a 6, six 3's, and seven 2's. Other good innings were played by Bird, G. George, and Page who drove one of Bacon's deliveries out of the field for 6. A word of praise ought to be given to Raffety among the younger members of the team, who played well for 21; his principal hits being a 4, three 3's, and three 2's. Bacon was the most successful in bowling, his eight wickets costing a trifle over six runs apiece, and the last three being obtained without a run being scored off him. For Wooburn Institute, Bacon, Bowler, and Plumridge played well, the second named hitting G. George for a 6. When stumps were drawn the visitors had made 129 for seven wickets, the last three of which had put on but eight runs between them. Page was the most successful with the ball, but his four wickets cost nearly 12 each. Score and analysis:—

MARLOW v. MR. J. MONRO WALKER'S XI.
On Saturday Marlow met an eleven got together by Mr. J Monro Walker, of Bisham Abbey, on the Marlow ground The weather was delightfully fine, and an enjoyable game resulted. The visitors won the toss, and took first innings. Harbottle hit hard for 80, and with smaller contributions from all the side except Lane (who was run out before he had scored), the total reached 183. Harbottle hit a 9 (four for an overthrow) and four 4's. Monro Walker was credited with an 8 (four for an overthrow). Marlow lost Paine and Faulkner cheaply, but with useful scores from Langley, Bower, Baillie, and Want, the visitors' total was passed with six wickets down. Eventually the innings closed for 183. Want—one of the Australian visitors staying in Marlow—hit a 5, six 4's, and three 3's in his dashing score of 48. Langley hit five 4's in his 30. Mr. Walker's team went in a second time, and had compiled 113 for six wickets, when stumps were drawn. Marlow therefore won by 30 runs on the first innings. Full score and analysis:—

WYCOMBE CHURCH ROOM v. WYCOMBE ST. JOHN'S.
The third encounter between the above-named teams took place on the Wycombe Rye on Saturday last in splendid weather, and, after a pleasant and interesting game, resulted in a win for the Church Room by 37 runs on the first innings. The St. John's won the toss and elected to bat first, and compiled the moderate total of 60, E. Free (12), Burnham (8), and Ing (8) being the top scorers. The Church Room then went in, and replied with 77, G. Vickers (not out, 26), Sexton (16), and C. Twitchen (13) being the double-figure contributors. The St. John's then went in again, and showed better form, knocking up 60, W. Rolls (11), Ing (12), and Ford (9) being the chief scorers. Twitchen and Vickers bowled well for the winners, while Rolls and Burnham were the best for the losers. Score:—

WYCOMBE BELLE VUE WANDERERS v. HOLLOWAY'S BOOT OPERATIVES C.C.
The return match between the above-named teams, which took place on the Wycombe Rye last Saturday, excited great interest. Mr. E. C. Spicer, who "skippered" the Wanderers, turned out a formidable eleven, while the shoemakers were but poorly represented, in fact at the last moment they had to make up with five substitutes. The men of "wax and leather" batted first, and ran up a creditable total of 66; Wilks, Humphrey, Collier, Lillyman, and Coles, contributing their respective scores in fine style. Tibbles, with the ball, was in rare form, his four wickets only costing a fraction over 4 runs a-piece; Anger took 2 wickets for 20. The time eventually arrived for the Wanderers' turn at the wicket, Coltman and Thorne opening the attack against the destructive deliveries of Humphrey and Mead. Wickets 1 and 2 went down for 14, and at this juncture it looked as though the Wanderers' contingent would collapse, six wickets being captured for 29, the last three of which not adding a run. The score rose slowly, and when Thorne went in the Wanderers' hopes revived, the great slogger piling on his 15 in double quick time. The end eventually arrived with the total at 54, which left the operatives winners on the first innings by 12 runs. Both Mead and Humphrey, who bowled throughout the game, captured 4 wickets each for 26 runs a-piece. The shoemen went in a second time, and at the close of the venture 31 runs had been added for the loss of seven wickets. After the match the teams heartily enjoyed a social at the "Belle Vue," Gordon-road. Score:—

SPEEN v. ICKENHAM.
This match was played at Speen, a good number of spectators being present to witness the play. It was felt by both teams that it would be a close shave, so each team entered the field ready to its best to win, but, after a very pleasant game, it was found that Speen had been beaten by 20 runs. The Speen Brass Band was present, and added to the pleasantness of the day by playing selections of music. A capital tea was provided by Mrs. Gomm for all who cared to partake, and altogether a thoroughly enjoyable day was the result of the club's effort. Score:—

MR. W. PEARCE'S (WYCOMBE) XI. v. SOUTHALL.
On Saturday last Mr. W. Pearce, of the "Nag's Head," London-road, captained an eleven to visit Southall to try conclusions with an eleven representing the Southall Gas Works. Although the Bucks men made a fine innings, having 112 runs to their credit, Southall were far and away the best team, and for the loss of only 3 wickets they had contributed 157 runs. Dixon and Hudson were said to be classed as belonging to the Middlesex team of Colts, and the way in which Dixon contributed his 76 showed that he was a batsman of no mean order. His total included one 5, three 4's, fifteen 3's, and five 2's. William Cooper, too, knocked up eight boundaries in succession. In fact, against such formidable opponents the bowling of the Wycombe representatives was taxed to its utmost; but, nevertheless, a pleasant game was the result. Both W. Pearce and C. W. Harper showed good form for the losers. Score and analysis:—

MR. COLLINS' CLASS v. BOOKER TEMPERANCE.
The return match between these clubs took place at Booker on Saturday last, and a pleasant game resulted in a win for the Class by eight runs on the first innings. The meeting of these teams has usually been a close game; last year it was a win for the Class and a drawn match, and this year the result of the fixtures has been the same. Batting first, the Class made 50, J. Keen (23) and Collins (10) being chief contributors. Booker then went in, and the total had reached 42 when the last wicket fell, out of which number Burnham had made 16. In their second venture the Class could only compile 27, neither batsman being able to make a stand against the under-arm bowling of C. Pearce; Heather (15) was the only one to get into double figures. Scores:—

MASTER H. PENTON'S XI. v. HEDGERLEY HOME.
A match was played at Chalfont Park on August 22nd, between XI. got together by Master H. Penton and XI. of the Church of England Waifs and Strays, Hedgerley Home, by invitation. The visitors were put in first, Watson batting well for 30, the whole team being soon dismissed for 66. For the home side Master H. Penton played a capital innings for 63 (not out) ; C. Roe and Ranschaert also batted well. Tea was provided on the grounds by Captain Penton, to which full justice was done, and a good afternoon's game was enjoyed. Score:—

CAMBS. CUP COMPETITION.
On Saturday the second round of the Cambs. Cup Competition was played on Parker's Piece, between the Old Higher Grade and Sawston. The match ended in an easy win for the Old Higher Grade by 190 runs. For Sawston, B Bailey was the only scorer, with five runs to his credit, extras being credited with six. For the Old Higher Grade, Cornell took six wickets for one run, and Luff four wickets for four runs. The following is the score :-

MARRIED V. SINGLE.
On Tuesday a second match was played upon the same ground between Eleven Married and Eleven Single, Mr Hoare himself taking the bat with the Married Eleven. It was a well contested game, the Single team being the victors by 5 runs only. F Baker was successful with both ball and bat. Refreshments were dispensed to players and spectators, and in the evening a substantial supper was provided for all that had taken part in the game. About 30 sat down, and Mr Hoare joined the company. The tables being cleared, Mr Blake, in appropriate words, proposed the health of the host, which was drunk with musical honours. A social and harmonious evening was spent, such as Sutton cricketers have not often the opportunity of spending. Score :-

CAMBRIDGE EXPRESS: SATURDAY 3 AUGUST 1895 - 3

SPORT AND PLAY.
GOSSIP UPON CURRENT SPORTS
AND PASTIMES.

I am vain enough to think that some of my
readers have missed "Vim's" notes from the
columns of the Express during the last fortnight.
To them I offer an apology for my non-appearance
in print. Like the majority of people, I caught
the election fever, and, becoming absorbed in the
progress of the fight, had no time to expend upon
such mundane things as athletic notes. I am
afraid I have rather got out of touch with the
progress of events in the athletic world during
the last fortnight, but will do my best to make up
lost ground.

My first duty is to express both pleasure and
regret at the doings of the County Cricket Club.
The drubbing the County team received from
the M.C.C. and Ground was a severe one, although
the Club team was not a particularly strong one.
These curious collapses of our County teams are
unexplainable by me, although those who are
behind the scenes may be able to give a
reason. With a somewhat stronger eleven, the
County gave Hunts. on Wednesday a ditto to the
treatment they had received from the M.C.C.,
viz., a single innings defeat. The record for the
season thus far is one win and one loss. On
Monday and Tuesday next, the County will
entertain the M.C.C. and Ground at Cambridge,
and it is to be hoped that they may be able to
give a better account of themselves then.

The old suggestion has been revived in the
select circle of enthusiasts of the game of the
desirability of playing at least one County match
each season upon Parker's Piece. The Hunts.
match was peculiarly suited to such treatment,
and it is a pity that it was not played on the
public ground, and used to excite a greater
interest amongst Cambridge people in the doings
of the Club, the future of which looks none too
rosy at present.

The final of the Cambridgeshire Cricket Cup
Competition will again be fought out by the Old
Higher Grade, last year's winners, and the
Camden. The old boys are such good sportsmen
that one would like to see them win again, but,
on the other hand, the Camden have been in the
competition since the very commencement, and
have had a great run of ill-luck, and their win
would be a popular one. The final promises once
more to be an extremely interesting one.

The scratching of the Cassandra Club in this
Competition has caused a good deal of public
comment. I have had a conversation with the
secretary, who declines to state why the Club
scratched, although he affirms that they had good
and sufficient reason for so doing, which I do not
doubt. After all, action of this kind is the Club's
private business, but it seems a pity the Cassandra
should have knocked out the old Perseans, who
would have gone through, and then have retired
without vouchsafing any reason for so doing.

I am really sorry for Sawston, who were so
crushingly defeated by the Old Higher Grade last
Saturday. What could have come over the
Institute team? The whole side was disposed of
for 11 runs, six of these being extras, and the only
man who scored off the bat was Bailey.

I am informed that the suggested dates for the
final are August 22nd and 23rd, but it has not
yet been decided whether the match shall be
played on Parker's Piece or the University
Ground.

CAMBRIDGE EXPRESS: SATURDAY 10 AUGUST 1895 - 2.

COUNTY v. BOROUGH POLICE.
The annual match between cricketing teams
representing the Borough and County of Cam-
bridge Police Forces took place on Wednesday,
when the policemen journeyed to Royston and
spent a pleasant time on the Heath. The County
went first to the wicket, and made 50, to which
p.-c. F. Brooks largely contributed. The Borough
team scored 68. Then followed a piece of good
cricket, in which the brothers p.-c.'s F. and G.
Brooks hit away in dashing style, and they were
so well supported by Inspector Webb and p.-c.
Carter that 69 runs for the loss of three wickets
were registered quickly, after which stumps were
drawn. The Borough thus obtained a victory on
the first innings. The bowling was chiefly
notable for p.-c. Rackham's analysis of 6 for 15
runs for the Borough, and p.-c. F. Brooks' 6 for
25 for the County. At the close of play the party
sat down to lunch at the White Horse. The
following is the score:--

SPORT AND PLAY.
GOSSIP UPON CURRENT SPORTS
AND PASTIMES.

A well-known writer on sport sends me the follow-
ing particulars of Kumar Shri Ranjitsinhji:—In
a memorable cricket season the performances of
K. S. Ranjitsinhji (as the famous Indian prefers
to be known, instead of as Prince) have created
almost as much attention as the doings of
the great "W. G." "Ranjit," as he is familiarly
called in University cricket, came over from
India some few seasons ago, and lived for a year
or so with the Rev. Louis Borissow, Precentor of
Trinity College. In October, 1889, he matriculated
as a Non-Coll. in the University of Cambridge,
but, though taking to cricket, few opportunities
presented themselves for displaying his abilities.
In due course he entered the foundation of
Trinity College, but excepting an occasional
match for the 2nd Eleven he was little known in
the cricket world until he became associated with
Cassandra and other Town Clubs, when he imme-
diately shot into prominence, and a great future
was predicted for him. In the year 1892, neither
'Varsity nor College could be induced to recognise
his sterling qualities. However, during that year
he had a magnificent average, and totalled over
2,000 runs, topping the century on 10 or 11
different occasions.

From the commencement of 1893 season his
exceptional prowess demanded the attention of the
'Varsity authorities, and Mr. Jackson awarded
him his blue, but although he averaged 29.72 in
'Varsity matches, in the Oxford and Cambridge
match he failed, as so many other great cricketers
have done. That year he was a regular member
of the Trinity 1st Eleven, and came out with the
fine figures of 71 8, eclipsing the batting achieve-
ments of Messrs. Jackson, W. G. Druce, Wells,
&c. His chief scores this season were 116,
111, 104, and 102 not out. He was appearing for
the County of Cambs. in the '93 and '94 seasons,
but from want of an extensive programme and
other causes did not shine very conspicuously.
He played in several first-class matches last
season and came out eighth, with an average of
32.03 for 16 innings, and altogether scored six cen-
turies, viz., 182, 146 not out, 137 not out, 123 not out,
115 not out, and 103 not out. While known but
little in first-class matches, his services during
last winter were sought by several counties, but
having a residential qualification for Sussex he
decided to throw in his lot with that county.
It will suffice to record the fact that this season,
up to August 3rd, he had totalled in all matches
2,117 runs, with an average of over 70, while in
first-class matches up to the date mentioned he
averaged 59.22, with an aggregate of 1,497, and
the following centuries figure in this large total of
206 not out, 174 not out, 150, 137 not out, 110, and
100. The last four centuries are first-class Space
will not permit of further reference to his efforts
with various other Clubs to which he belongs. On
his day he is able to send down a good ball, and
his early fame was established through his
brilliant fielding at short slip.

K. S. Ranjitsinhji, born in September, 1872, is
the second son of the Jam of Navanagar, and is,
therefore, in his 23rd year. His principal home
in this country is Cambridge, where, during the
winter months, he diligently participates in shoot-
ing and fishing. He is also a very good billiard
player, and good judges have asserted that had he
have taken more keenly to tennis and racquets he
would have represented his 'Varsity against
Oxford in either pastime.

Ranjitsinhji, whose mode of living is an ex-
ample which might well be followed by a num-
ber of cricketers, being a non-smoker and almost
total abstainer, at the same time is one of the
most jovial and unassuming fellows to meet; a
keen supporter of all legitimate recreation, a
severe critic on cricket, and very enthusiastic
in all sport he indulges in.

Whether K. S. Ranjitsinhji returns to his
native province at the end of this season re-
mains to be seen. However, it is contended that
he is too far infatuated and too great an exponent
of cricket to be able to tear himself from a
game in which he is so conspicuous at the present
moment, and the wish of all sportsman is at least
England will witness his prowess for many years
to come.

The County of Cambs. Cricket Eleven cannot
get steer clear of rough luck, and had it been
possible to complete the return match with
M.C.C and Ground, possibly they would have
experienced considerable trouble in saving the
game. Had the Marylebone Club batted under
the same conditions as Cambs. they would not
have made 243. The two Batters (who are likely
to be most useful for the County), Barnes' 118, and
Devey batted well, especially the Notts. veteran.
W. G. Grace, junr., who captured the M.C.C.
eleven, bowled with success.

Shortly the final tie for the Cambs. Cricket
Association Cup will be played, the contesting
Clubs being the holders--the Old Higher Grade--
and the Camden. Both Clubs command the
respect of all votaries of the game, and the victory
of either will be popular. The Camden, it is
stated, have never given the Association any
trouble, and have always been loyal to the
Committee. They have frequently figured in the
final stages, and are fully deserving of meeting
with success. This equally applies to the "Old
Boys," for whom P. Cornell has accomplished
some truly wonderful feats with the ball of late,
capturing six wickets for one run and seven
for ten.

For them P. Luff is also a useful performer, and
many think both he and Cornell should have
received trials for the County. For the Camden
O'Connor is the main cause for hope. Against
Hunts. the county "pro." actually captured 11
wickets for 30 runs. Should he be able to repeat
his best efforts the "Old Boys" would have any-
thing but an easy task.

Several fairly good bats appear for each eleven,
and everything points to an interesting game, and
we hope the game will permit of the best side
winning.

K. S. Ranjitsinhji informs me he he will not be
able to play any local cricket till after the Sussex
programme is completed, when he hopes to be
able to take part in afternoon matches.

The leading dozen batsmen and their averages
at the commencement of the week were:
                                Times   Most

The changes from the previous week were that
A. E. Stoddart and G. Brann qualified for the
first dozen, H. W. Bainbridge and H. K. Foster
making way. The old Etonian, however, is the
third Cambridge man to score 1,000 runs in first-
class matches. Such a feat may have previously
been accomplished, but I never heard of it, and
F. S. Jackson was the only Cambridge man to
reach those figures last year with 1020 for 39
innings. As N. F Druce, Lord Hawke, Hayward,
Carpenter, and F. S. Jackson have several more
matches to play, it is quite possible they may join
Messrs. Ranjitsinhji, Woods, and Bainbridge.

There is every prospect of Tom Hayward
going out to South Africa with George Lohmann's
team at the end of the season. I hear Tom is
anxious to bring a team down to Cambridge at
the end of the season. There was some talk of a
match last April between K. S Ranjitsinhji's XI.
and Tom Hayward's. Such a fixture in Septem-
ber, with strong sides, should prove a great
attraction.
